Q3 Results </B></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">DEERFIELD, Ill. &#150; Oct. 30, 2017 &#150; Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. (NASDAQ: MDLZ) today reported its third quarter 2017 results.
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;We&#146;re pleased with our improving revenue growth, driven by the strength of our Power Brands, continued momentum in emerging
markets and Europe,&#148; said Irene Rosenfeld, Chairman and CEO. &#147;We posted another quarter of strong expansion in operating income margin and earnings. We&#146;re making good progress on many of our key strategic initiatives and remain
confident in our ability to deliver long-term, sustainable growth on both the top and bottom lines.&#148; </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:11pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Net Revenue </B></P>

</TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I><U>Third Quarter Commentary</U> </I></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><B>Net revenues</B> increased 2.1&nbsp;percent, driven by Organic Net Revenue growth and currency tailwinds. Organic Net Revenue increased 2.8&nbsp;percent, driven by the continued strength of our Power Brands as well
as strong performance in Europe and emerging markets. The company also realized an estimated net positive impact of 60 basis points from delayed shipments that moved to the third quarter as the company recovered from the malware incident.
</TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><B>Gross profit margin</B> was 39.1&nbsp;percent, an increase of 20 basis points, driven primarily by lower Restructuring Program implementation costs and favorable <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> comparisons, partially offset by malware-related expenses. Adjusted Gross Profit margin was 39.5&nbsp;percent, a decrease of 60 basis points, driven by higher input costs and select trade
investments in some key markets, partially offset by continued net productivity gains. </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><B>Operating income margin</B> was 18.1&nbsp;percent, up 710 basis points, driven primarily by the gain on divestiture, the benefit from resolution of a Brazilian indirect tax matter and lower Restructuring Program
costs. Adjusted Operating Income margin increased 130 basis points to 16.9&nbsp;percent, due primarily to lower overhead costs driven by continued cost reduction efforts. </TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><B>Diluted EPS</B> was $0.65, up 86&nbsp;percent, driven primarily by the gain on divestiture, the benefit from resolution of a Brazilian indirect tax matter, lower Restructuring Program costs and operating gains.
</TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><B>Adjusted EPS</B> was $0.57 and grew 12&nbsp;percent on a constant-currency basis, driven primarily by operating gains. </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><B>Capital Return</B>: The company repurchased more than $700&nbsp;million of its common stock and paid approximately $300&nbsp;million in cash dividends. </TD></TR></TABLE>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">2 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>2017 Outlook </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Mondel&#275;z International provides guidance on a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> basis, as the company cannot predict some
elements that are included in reported GAAP results, including the impact of foreign exchange. Refer to the Outlook section in the discussion of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures below for more details. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">For 2017, the company now expects Organic Net Revenue growth to be approximately 1&nbsp;percent given the larger than expected impact from the
malware incident. The company still expects Adjusted Operating Income margin in the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mid-16&nbsp;percent</FONT> range and double-digit Adjusted EPS growth on a constant-currency basis. The company estimates full year
currency translation would not result in a change to net revenue growth or Adjusted EPS<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">3</SUP>. In addition, the company still expects Free Cash
Flow<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1</SUP> of approximately $2&nbsp;billion. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">3 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Conference Call </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Mondel&#275;z International will host a conference call for investors with accompanying slides to review its results at 5 p.m. ET today. A
listen-only webcast will be provided at <U>www.mondelezinternational.com</U>. An archive of the webcast will be available on the company&#146;s web site. The company will be live tweeting the event at <U>www.twitter.com/MDLZ</U>. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>About Mondel&#275;z International </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. (NASDAQ: MDLZ) is building the best snacking company in the world, with 2016 net revenues of approximately
$26&nbsp;billion. Creating more moments of joy in approximately 165 countries, Mondel&#275;z International is a world leader in biscuits, chocolate, gum, candy and powdered beverages, featuring global Power Brands such as <I>Oreo </I>and<I> belVita
</I>biscuits<I>; Cadbury Dairy Milk</I> and <I>Milka</I> chocolate; and <I>Trident</I> gum.&nbsp;Mondel&#275;z International is a proud member of the Standard and Poor&#146;s 500, NASDAQ 100 and Dow Jones Sustainability Index. Visit
<U>www.mondelezinternational.com</U> or follow the company on Twitter at <U>www.twitter.com/MDLZ</U>. </P> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">Net earnings attributable to Mondel&#275;z International. </TD></TR></TABLE>

</B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Power Brands include some of the company&#146;s largest global and regional brands, such as <I>Oreo</I>, <I>Chips Ahoy!</I>, <I>Ritz,
TUC/Club Social</I> and <I>belVita</I> biscuits; <I>Cadbury Dairy Milk, Milka</I> and <I>Lacta</I> chocolate; <I>Trident</I> gum; <I>Halls</I> candy; and <I>Tang</I> powdered beverages. </P>

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Emerging markets consist of the Latin America region in its entirety; the Asia, Middle East and
Africa region excluding Australia, New Zealand and Japan; and the following countries from the Europe region: Russia, Ukraine, Turkey, Kazakhstan, Belarus, Georgia, Poland, Czech Republic, Slovak Republic, Hungary, Bulgaria, Romania, the Baltics and
the East Adriatic countries. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Developed markets include the entire North America region, the Europe region excluding the countries
included in the emerging markets definition, and Australia, New Zealand and Japan from the Asia, Middle East and Africa region.</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Forward-Looking

 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">8 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:14pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. and Subsidiaries </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:12pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>Reconciliation of GAAP and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> Financial Measures </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:12pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>(Unaudited) </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company reports its
financial results in accordance with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States (&#147;GAAP&#148;). However, management believes that also presenting certain <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures
provides additional information to facilitate comparison of the company&#146;s historical operating results and trends in its underlying operating results, and provides additional transparency on how the company evaluates its business. Management
uses these <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures in making financial, operating and planning decisions and in evaluating the company&#146;s performance. The company also believes that presenting these measures allows
investors to view its performance using the same measures that the company uses in evaluating its financial and business performance and trends. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The
company considers quantitative and qualitative factors in assessing whether to adjust for the impact of items that may be significant or that could affect an understanding of its ongoing financial and business performance and trends. The adjustments
generally fall within the following categories: acquisition&nbsp;&amp; divestiture activities, gains and losses on intangible asset sales and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> impairments, major program restructuring activities,
constant currency and related adjustments, major program financing and hedging activities and other major items affecting comparability of operating results. See below for a description of adjustments to the company&#146;s U.S. GAAP financial
measures included herein. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> information should be considered as supplemental in nature and is not meant to
be considered in isolation or as a substitute for the related financial information prepared in accordance with U.S. GAAP. In addition, the company&#146;s <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures may not be the same as or
comparable to similar <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measures presented by other companies. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Because GAAP financial measures on a
forward-looking basis are not accessible and reconciling information is not available without unreasonable effort, the company has not provided that information with regard to the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures
in the company&#146;s outlook. Refer to the Outlook section below for more details. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">9 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>DEFINITIONS OF THE COMPANY&#146;S <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">NON-GAAP</FONT> FINANCIAL MEASURES </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company&#146;s <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures and corresponding metrics reflect how the company evaluates its
operating results currently and provide improved comparability of operating results. As new events or circumstances arise, these definitions could change over time. When these definitions change, the company provides the updated definitions and
presents the related <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> historical results on a comparable basis <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(1)</SUP>. </P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">&#147;Organic Net Revenue&#148; is defined as net revenues excluding the impacts of acquisitions; divestitures <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(2)</SUP>; the historical global coffee business <SUP
STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(3)</SUP>; the historical Venezuelan operations; accounting calendar changes; and currency rate fluctuations <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(4)</SUP>. The company believes that Organic Net
Revenue reflects the underlying growth from the ongoing activities of its business and provides improved comparability of results. The company also evaluates Organic Net Revenue growth from emerging markets and its Power Brands. </TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">&#147;Adjusted Gross Profit&#148; is defined as gross profit excluding the 2012-2014 Restructuring Program <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(5)</SUP>; the 2014-2018 Restructuring Program <SUP
STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(5)</SUP>; acquisition integration costs; incremental costs associated with the Jacobs Douwe Egberts (&#147;JDE&#148;) coffee business transactions; the operating results of divestitures <SUP
STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(2)</SUP>; the historical coffee business operating results <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(3)</SUP>; the historical Venezuelan operating results; and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT

margin,&#148; which is subject to the same adjustments as Adjusted Gross Profit. The company believes that Adjusted Gross Profit and Adjusted Gross Profit margin provide improved comparability of underlying operating results. The company also
evaluates growth in the company&#146;s Adjusted Gross Profit on a constant currency basis <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(4)</SUP>. </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

divestitures <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(2)</SUP>; the historical global coffee business operating results <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(3)</SUP>;
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts from commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivative contracts <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(6)</SUP>; equity method

Segment Operating Income. The company believes that Adjusted Operating Income, Adjusted Segment Operating Income, Adjusted Operating Income margin and Adjusted Segment Operating Income margin provide improved comparability of underlying operating
results. The company also evaluates growth in the company&#146;s Adjusted Operating Income and Adjusted Segment Operating Income on a constant currency basis <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(4)</SUP>. </TD></TR></TABLE>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">During the third quarter of 2016, the company began to exclude unrealized gains and losses <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">(mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts) from outstanding
commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivatives from its <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> earnings measures until such time that the related exposures impact its operating results. Since the company purchases commodity and
forecasted currency contracts to mitigate price volatility primarily for inventory requirements in future periods, the company made this adjustment to remove the volatility of these future inventory purchases on current operating results to
facilitate comparisons of its underlying operating performance across periods. The company also discontinued designating commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivatives for hedge accounting treatment. To facilitate comparisons of the
company&#146;s underlying operating results, the company has recast all historical <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> earnings measures to exclude the
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts. </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>SEGMENT OPERATING INCOME </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company uses segment operating income to evaluate segment performance and allocate resources. The company believes it is appropriate to disclose this
measure to help investors analyze segment performance and trends. Segment operating income excludes unrealized gains and losses on hedging activities (which are a component of cost of sales), general corporate expenses (which are a component of
selling, general and administrative expenses), amortization of intangibles and gains and losses on divestitures in all periods presented. The company excludes these items from segment operating income in order to provide better transparency of its
segment operating results. Furthermore, the company centrally manages interest and other expense, net. Accordingly, the company does not present these items by segment because they are excluded from the segment profitability measure that management
reviews. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>ITEMS IMPACTING COMPARABILITY OF OPERATING RESULTS </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The following information is provided to give qualitative and quantitative information related to items impacting comparability of operating results. The
company determines which items to consider as &#147;items impacting comparability&#148; based on how management views the company&#146;s business; makes financial, operating and planning decisions; and evaluates the company&#146;s ongoing
performance. In addition, the company discloses the impact of changes in currency exchange rates on the company&#146;s financial results in order to reflect results on a constant currency basis. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Divestitures, Divestiture-related costs and Gains/(losses) on divestitures </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On October&nbsp;2, 2017, the company completed the sale of one of its equity method investments. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In connection with the 2012 <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">spin-off</FONT> of Kraft Foods Group, Inc. (now a part of KHC), Kraft Foods Group and the company
each granted the other various licenses to use certain trademarks in connection with particular product categories in specified jurisdictions. On August&nbsp;17, 2017, the company entered into two agreements with KHC to terminate the licenses of
certain <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">KHC-owned</FONT> brands used in the company&#146;s grocery business within its Europe region and to transfer to KHC inventory and certain other assets. On August&nbsp;17, 2017, the first transaction closed,
and on October&nbsp;23, 2017, the second transaction closed. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On July&nbsp;4, 2017, the company completed the sale of most of its grocery business in
Australia and New Zealand to Bega Cheese Limited.&nbsp;The company recorded a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain of $247&nbsp;million Australian dollars ($187&nbsp;million as of July&nbsp;4, 2017) on the sale during the three
months ended September&nbsp;30, 2017. The company incurred divestiture-related costs of $2&nbsp;million in the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2017. The company also had a gain on a foreign currency hedge of $2&nbsp;million in the three months and a
net loss of $3&nbsp;million in the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2017. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On April&nbsp;28, 2017, the company completed the sale of several
manufacturing facilities in France and the sale or license of several local confectionery brands. The company recorded a $3&nbsp;million loss on the sale during the three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2017. The company incurred divestiture-related
costs of $1&nbsp;million in the three months and $22&nbsp;million in the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2017 and no divestiture-related costs in the three months and $84&nbsp;million in the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2016. The
company recorded these costs within cost of sales and selling, general and administrative expenses of its Europe segment. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On December&nbsp;1, 2016, the
company completed the sale of a confectionery business in Costa Rica represented by a local brand. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Acquisitions </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On November&nbsp;2, 2016, the company purchased from Burton&#146;s Biscuit Company certain intangibles, which included the license to manufacture, market and
sell Cadbury-branded biscuits in additional key markets around the world, including in the United Kingdom, France, Ireland, North America and Saudi Arabia. On a constant currency basis, the purchase added incremental net revenues of $20&nbsp;million
in the three months and $50&nbsp;million in the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2017. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Acquisition integration costs </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Within the company&#146;s AMEA segment, in connection with the acquisition of a biscuit operation in Vietnam, the company recorded integration costs of
$1&nbsp;million in the three months and $2&nbsp;million in the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2017 and $6&nbsp;million in the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2016. The company recorded these acquisition integration costs in selling,
general and administrative expenses. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">12 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>2014-2018 Restructuring Program </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On May&nbsp;6, 2014, the company&#146;s Board of Directors approved a $3.5&nbsp;billion restructuring program and up to $2.2&nbsp;billion of capital
expenditures. On August&nbsp;31, 2016, the company&#146;s Board of Directors approved a $600&nbsp;million reallocation between restructuring program cash costs and capital expenditures so that now the $5.7&nbsp;billion program consists of
approximately $4.1&nbsp;billion of restructuring program costs ($3.1&nbsp;billion cash costs and $1&nbsp;billion <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> costs) and up to $1.6&nbsp;billion of capital expenditures. The primary objective of
the 2014-2018 Restructuring Program is to reduce the company&#146;s operating cost structure in both its supply chain and overhead costs. The program is intended primarily to cover severance as well as asset disposals and other manufacturing-related
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">one-time</FONT> costs. Since inception, the company has incurred total restructuring and related implementation charges of $3.1&nbsp;billion related to the 2014-2018 Restructuring Program. The company expects to
incur the full $4.1&nbsp;billion of program charges by <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-end</FONT> 2018. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Restructuring costs </I></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company recorded restructuring charges of $113&nbsp;million in the three months and $418&nbsp;million in the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2017 and
$187&nbsp;million in the three months and $480&nbsp;million in the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2016 within asset impairment and exit costs. These charges were for <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> asset write-downs (including
accelerated depreciation and asset impairments), severance and other related costs. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Implementation costs </I></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Implementation costs are directly attributable to restructuring activities; however, they do not qualify for special accounting treatment as exit or disposal
activities. Implementation costs primarily relate to reorganizing the company&#146;s operations and facilities in connection with its supply chain reinvention program and other identified productivity and cost saving initiatives. The costs include
incremental expenses related to the closure of facilities, costs to terminate certain contracts and the simplification of the company&#146;s information systems. The company recorded implementation costs of $62&nbsp;million in the three months and
$179&nbsp;million in the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2017 and $114&nbsp;million in the three months and $286&nbsp;million in the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2016. The company recorded these costs within cost of sales and general
corporate expense within selling, general and administrative expenses. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Gain on equity method investment exchange </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On March&nbsp;3, 2016, a subsidiary of Acorn Holdings B.V. (&#147;AHBV&#148;) completed the $13.9&nbsp;billion acquisition of all of the outstanding common
stock of Keurig Green Mountain, Inc. (&#147;Keurig&#148;) through a merger transaction. On March&nbsp;7, 2016, the company exchanged with a subsidiary of AHBV a portion of the company&#146;s equity interest in JDE with a carrying value of
&#128;1.7&nbsp;billion (approximately $2.0&nbsp;billion as of March&nbsp;7, 2016) for an interest in Keurig with a fair value of $2.0&nbsp;billion based on the merger consideration per share for Keurig. The company recorded the difference between
the fair value of Keurig and its basis in JDE shares as a $43&nbsp;million gain on the equity method investment exchange in March 2016. Immediately following the exchange, the company&#146;s ownership interest in JDE was 26.5% and its interest in
Keurig was 24.2%. The company accounts for its investments in JDE and Keurig under the equity method and recognizes its share of their earnings within equity method investment earnings and its share of their dividends within the company&#146;s cash
flows. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Equity method investee adjustments </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Within Adjusted EPS, the company&#146;s equity method investment net earnings exclude its proportionate share of its investees&#146; unusual or infrequent
items, such as acquisition and divestiture-related costs and restructuring program costs. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts from commodity and currency derivative contracts </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the third quarter of 2016,
the company began to exclude unrealized gains and losses <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">(mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts) from outstanding commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivatives from its <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> earnings measures until such time that the related exposures impact its operating results. To facilitate comparisons of its underlying operating results, the company has recast all historical <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> earnings measures to exclude the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company recorded net unrealized gains on commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivatives of $28&nbsp;million in the three months and net
unrealized losses of $69&nbsp;million in the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2017 and net unrealized losses of $12&nbsp;million in the three months and $49&nbsp;million in the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2016. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">13 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Loss related to interest rate swaps </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company recognized <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> losses of $97&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2016, within
interest and other expense, net related to certain U.S. dollar interest rate swaps that the company no longer designated as accounting cash flow hedges due to a change in financing plans. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Loss on debt extinguishment </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On April&nbsp;12,
2017, the company discharged $488&nbsp;million of its 6.500% U.S. dollar-denominated debt. The company paid $504&nbsp;million, representing principal as well as past and future interest accruals from February 2017 through the August 2017 maturity
date. The company recorded an $11&nbsp;million loss on debt extinguishment within interest expense. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Intangible assets gains and losses </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Impairment charges </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the company&#146;s annual
testing of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-amortizable</FONT> intangible assets, the company recorded $70&nbsp;million of impairment charges in the third quarter of 2017 related to five trademarks. The impairments arose due to lower than
expected growth in part driven by decisions to redirect support from these trademarks to other regional and global brands. The company recorded charges related to candy and gum trademarks of $52&nbsp;million in AMEA, $11&nbsp;million in Europe,
$5&nbsp;million in Latin America and $2&nbsp;million in North America. In addition, during the third quarter of 2017, the company recorded a $1&nbsp;million impairment related to a transaction. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the second quarter of 2017, the company recorded a $38&nbsp;million intangible asset impairment charge resulting from a category decline and lower than
expected product growth related to a gum trademark in its North America segment. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2016, the company
discontinued one biscuit product that resulted in a $4&nbsp;million intangible asset impairment charge in its Europe segment. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On June&nbsp;30, 2016, in
connection with the company&#146;s global supply chain reinvention initiatives, the company made a determination to discontinue manufacturing a candy product that resulted in a $7&nbsp;million impairment charge in its North America segment. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On March&nbsp;31, 2016, in connection with the sale of a confectionery business in France, the company recorded a $14&nbsp;million impairment charge for a
gum&nbsp;&amp; candy trademark as a portion of its carrying value would not be recoverable based on future cash flows expected under a planned license agreement with the buyer. In May 2016, the company recorded an additional $5&nbsp;million
impairment charge for a candy trademark to reduce the overall net assets to the estimated net sales proceeds after transaction costs. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Gain on sale of
an intangible asset </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On August&nbsp;26, 2016, the company recorded a $7&nbsp;million gain for the sale of a U.S.-owned biscuit trademark. The gain was
recorded within selling, general and administrative expenses of its North America segment. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On May&nbsp;2, 2016, the company completed the sale of certain
local biscuit brands in Finland as part of the company&#146;s strategic decisions to exit select small and local brands and shift investment toward its Power Brands. The sales price was &#128;14&nbsp;million ($16&nbsp;million as of May&nbsp;2, 2016)
and the company divested $8&nbsp;million of indefinite lived intangible assets and less than $1&nbsp;million of other assets. The company received cash proceeds of &#128;12&nbsp;million ($14&nbsp;million as of May&nbsp;2, 2016) and another
&#128;2&nbsp;million ($2&nbsp;million as of October&nbsp;31, 2016) following the completion of post-closing requirements. The additional $2&nbsp;million of consideration increased the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain of
$6&nbsp;million recorded in the second quarter of 2016 to a total 2016 <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain of $8&nbsp;million. This transaction was recorded within selling, general and administrative expenses of the company&#146;s
Europe segment. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Incremental expenses related to the malware incident </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On June&nbsp;27, 2017, a global malware incident impacted the company&#146;s business. The malware affected a significant portion of the company&#146;s global
sales, distribution and financial networks. During the last four days of the second quarter and early third quarter, the company executed business continuity and contingency plans to contain the impact and minimize the damages and restore its
systems environment. The company does not expect, nor to date has it found, any instances of Company or personal data released externally. The company restored its main operating systems and processes and continues to further enhance the security of
its systems. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">For the second quarter, the company estimates that the malware incident had a negative impact of 2.3% on its net revenue growth and 2.4% on
its Organic Net Revenue growth. While the company is pleased with its recovery </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">14 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">
efforts following the malware incident, restoring North America systems has taken longer, resulting in additional lost revenue for the year. As a result, for the third quarter, the company
estimates that the recovery of shipments delayed due to the malware incident had a net favorable impact of 0.6% on its net revenue and Organic Net Revenue growth. The company also incurred incremental expenses of $47&nbsp;million as a result of the
incident in the three months and $54&nbsp;million in the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2017. The company expects to incur additional incremental expenses related to the incident and recovery process during the fourth quarter of 2017. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Benefit from resolution of tax matters </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the
first quarter of 2017, the Brazilian Supreme Court (the &#147;Court&#148;) ruled against the Brazilian tax authorities in a leading case related to the computation of certain indirect <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">(non-income)</FONT> taxes. The
Court ruled that the indirect tax base should not include a value-added tax known as &#147;ICMS&#148;. By removing the ICMS from the tax base, the Court effectively eliminated a &#147;tax on a tax.&#148; The company&#146;s Brazilian subsidiary had
received an injunction against making payments for the &#147;tax on a tax&#148; in 2008 and since that time until December 2016, the company had accrued for this portion of the tax each quarter in the event that the tax was reaffirmed by the
Brazilian courts. On September&nbsp;30, 2017, based on legal advice and the publication of the Court&#146;s decision related to this case, the company determined that the likelihood that the increased tax base would be reinstated and assessed
against the company was remote. Accordingly, the company reversed its accrual of 667&nbsp;million Brazilian reais, or $212&nbsp;million as of September&nbsp;30, 2017, of which, $153&nbsp;million was recorded within selling, general and
administrative expenses and $59&nbsp;million was recorded within interest and other expense, net. The Brazilian tax authority may appeal the Court&#146;s decision, seeking potential clarification or adjustment of the terms of enforcement. The
company continues to monitor developments in this matter and currently does not expect a material future impact on its financial statements. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">As part of
the company&#146;s 2010 Cadbury acquisition, the company became the responsible party for tax matters under a February&nbsp;2, 2006 dated Deed of Tax Covenant between the Cadbury Schweppes PLC and related entities (&#147;Schweppes&#148;) and Black
Lion Beverages and related entities. The tax matters included an ongoing transfer pricing case with the Spanish tax authorities related to the Schweppes businesses Cadbury divested prior to the company&#146;s acquisition of Cadbury. During the first
quarter of 2017, the Spanish Supreme Court decided the case in the company&#146;s favor. As a result of the final ruling, during the first quarter of 2017, the company recorded a favorable earnings impact of $46&nbsp;million in selling, general and
administrative expenses and $12&nbsp;million in interest and other expense, net, for a total <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> impact of $58&nbsp;million due to the reversal of Cadbury-related accrued liabilities related to this
matter. In the third quarter of 2017, we recorded additional income of $3&nbsp;million related to a bank guarantee release within selling, general and administrative expenses and interest and other expense, net. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Constant currency </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Management evaluates the
operating performance of the company and its international subsidiaries on a constant currency basis. The company determines its constant currency operating results by dividing or multiplying, as appropriate, the current period local currency
operating results by the currency exchange rates used to translate the company&#146;s financial statements in the comparable prior-year period to determine what the current period U.S. dollar operating results would have been if the currency
exchange rate had not changed from the comparable prior-year period. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>OUTLOOK </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company&#146;s outlook for 2017 Organic Net Revenue growth, Adjusted Operating Income margin, Adjusted EPS growth on a constant currency basis and Free
Cash Flow are <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures that exclude or otherwise adjust for items impacting comparability of financial results such as the impact of changes in foreign currency exchange rates, restructuring
activities, acquisitions and divestitures. The company is not able to reconcile its full year 2017 projected Organic Net Revenue growth to its full year 2017 projected reported net revenue growth because the company is unable to predict the 2017
impact of foreign exchange due to the unpredictability of future changes in foreign exchange rates, which could be material as a significant portion of the company&#146;s operations are outside the U.S. The company is not able to reconcile its full
year 2017 projected Adjusted Operating Income margin to its full year 2017 projected reported operating income margin because the company is unable to predict the timing of its Restructuring Program costs, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts from commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivative contracts and impacts from potential acquisitions or divestitures. The company is not able to reconcile its full year 2017
projected Adjusted EPS growth on a constant currency basis to its full year 2017 projected reported diluted EPS growth because the company is unable to predict the timing of its Restructuring Program costs, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts from commodity and forecasted currency forecasted derivative contracts, impacts from potential acquisitions or divestitures as well as the impact of foreign exchange due to the
unpredictability of future changes in </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">15 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">
foreign exchange rates, which could be material as a significant portion of the company&#146;s operations are outside the U.S. The company is not able to reconcile its full year 2017 projected
Free Cash Flow to its full year 2017 projected net cash from operating activities because the company is unable to predict the timing and amount of capital expenditures impacting cash flow. Therefore, because of the uncertainty and variability of
the nature and amount of future adjustments, which could be significant, the company is unable to provide a reconciliation of these measures without unreasonable effort. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">16 </P>
